################################################################################
# ROUND 5 SCHEDULING ANALYSIS - FAIR COMPARISON (GROUP_SIZE=10, N_SETS=2)
################################################################################

METRIC EXPLANATIONS
===================
Each instruction shows metrics as: (dist_to_load, -dist_to_pause, order, direct_users, transitive_unique_users, slack)

1. dist_to_load
   - Shortest path distance from this node to a LOAD operation (via users)
   - Lower = closer to enabling a memory load = higher scheduling priority
   - LOAD nodes have dist_to_load = 0
   - Used as PRIMARY sort key (ascending)

2. -dist_to_pause (negated)
   - Longest path distance from this node to a pause/barrier node
   - Higher magnitude = earlier in critical path = should be scheduled sooner
   - Shown negated so higher values have higher priority
   - Used as SECONDARY sort key (descending, hence negation)

3. order
   - Original emission order when the instruction was added to the AST
   - Used as TERTIARY sort key for stability (ascending)
   - Lower order = emitted earlier in code generation

4. direct_users
   - Number of nodes that directly depend on this node
   - Higher = more immediate downstream work unlocked when scheduled

5. transitive_unique_users
   - Total number of unique nodes reachable downstream (transitive closure)
   - Higher = more total work eventually depends on this node
   - Key indicator of "importance" in the dependency graph

6. slack
   - How much this node can be delayed without affecting total completion time
   - slack = critical_path_length - earliest_start - dist_to_sink
   - Higher slack = more scheduling freedom, can be delayed
   - Lower slack = on or near critical path, should be scheduled promptly

INTERPRETATION
==============
- Operations marked with *** are the target group/round being analyzed
- In the PREVIOUS (round-by-round) code, Group 1 ops have HIGH slack (~149) and
  LOW transitive_users (~600), indicating they are NOT on the critical path
- In the CURRENT (stage-based) code, Group 1 ops have LOW slack (~13) and
  HIGH transitive_users (~2100), indicating tighter coupling in the DAG
- The round-by-round emission creates asymmetric dependencies that allow better
  interleaving; stage-based emission creates homogeneous dependencies
